y s t a l growth d u r i n g t h e w i r e drawing p r o c e s s .\n\nSince t h i s\n\nwas beyond t h e scope of contractNAS3-7106, TRW Systems w a s asked t o and d i d\npropose a follow-on program f o r f u r t h e r s t u d i e s w i t h b e r y l l i u m .\n\nHowever, t h e\n\nf u n d i n g f o r t h i s work w a s c a n c e l l e d b e f o r e a c o n t r a c t w a s awarded.\nS i x l i f e t o t a l r a d i a t i o n l o s s . w a s t h e r e f o r e o n l y 46%.\n\n123\n\n(1).\n\nBecause of the significance of these measurements in terms of power\nefficiency for the ion emitter, TRW Systems undertook an in-house investigation to check the reliability of the data and determine where shielding\nefficiency could be improved.\nThese experiments were conducted with a reject emitter whose heating requirements were measured before and after electropolishing. A total\nof 32 different measurements with different shielding configurations reconfirmed the emissivity measurements above for freshly electropolished porous\ntungsten. Further, it was found that thermal efficiency could be increased\nto 60% fairly easily.\nA more definitive experiment was performed by electropolishing\n\nemitter 6-7-3 (Hughes 324-S material) and using a shielding configuration\nconsisting of rhodium heat shield boxes close to the emitter plus a 1/4"\nthick layer of fibrafrax and a final outer covering of molybdenum. The\nmeasured heating requirement was 137 watts at 1 0 \' .\n50K\nThis power requirement is plotted as a function of temperature in\nFigure 56 and labelled "present heating requirement". Comparing this with\nthe power requirements of the various emitters tested under this contract\n(also plotted in Figure 56) shows the significant improvement which has\nbeen achieved. Further improvements should lead to the "future heating\nrequirement" curve which represents a thermal shielding efficiency of\n\n72% (i.e. frontal radiation accounts for 72% of the total loss).\nThe heat shielding experiments also isolated various sources\nof heat loss. This is due to the elimination of the remnant-oxygen contamination.\n\nIn both cases we have used engine data for a vs T character-\n\nistics of G-4 material. Case (3) shows the additional efficiency\nimprovement obtainable if the low neutrals and operating temperatures\nof the button data can be duplicated by a large emitter such as 6-7-3.\nNote that the electrical efficiency has increased from 67 to 80.6% and\nthe electrode life has also increased by almost 15%.\n\n8.4 DURABILITY VERSUS EFFICIENCY FOR VARIOUS SELECTED IONIZER MATERIALS\nIn order to estimate the present state of the art of contact ion\nengines we have calculated the ev/ion requirement for several of the better\nmaterials which have been tested in the past two years.
